# AI-First Game Development Roadmap
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
**Status:** Living document. Updated whenever a spec lands or scope shifts.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
**Vision:** civ-engine should support an environment where AI agents do as much game-development work as possible without human intervention ╨ô?" generating, exercising, debugging, and verifying game logic autonomously, with humans involved only for design intent and judgment calls. This document captures the multi-spec roadmap that delivers that environment.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
A single recording-and-replay spec is the substrate. The full vision spans nine specs across three tiers; specs are tracked individually under `docs/design/<date>-<topic>-design.md`.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
## Tier 1 ╨ô?" Foundational
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
Without these, "AI-first" is aspirational. They are the irreducible substrate for autonomous feedback loops.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
### Spec 1: Session Recording & Replay (engine primitives)
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
Status: **Drafted 2026-04-26.** See `2026-04-26-session-recording-and-replay-design.md`.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
What it delivers: deterministic capture of any World run as a portable `SessionBundle`; replay engine that opens a paused World at any tick; marker API for human and programmatic annotations; sink interface for memory and disk persistence; unification with `ScenarioRunner` so test runs and live captures share the same bundle format and replayer.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
What it unlocks: every other spec in this roadmap.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
### Spec 3: Synthetic Playtest Harness
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
Status: **Proposed.**
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
What it delivers: a harness that constructs a `World`, attaches a `SessionRecorder`, drives `world.submit()` from a pluggable policy (random / scripted / LLM-driven / heuristic agents), runs for N ticks, and saves the bundle. Trivially parallelizable across cores or machines. Produces a corpus of bundles per commit.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
What it unlocks: the actual feedback loop. Without synthetic playtest, recording just makes human bug reports nicer; with it, every commit gets autonomous exploration. Agents review the corpus and self-file regressions before any human plays the game.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
Why it depends on Spec 1: synthetic playtest is just "policy ╨ô+' submit() ╨ô+' SessionBundle"; without recording there is no artifact to analyze.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
### Spec 8: Behavioral Metrics over Corpus
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
Status: **Proposed.**
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
What it delivers: a metrics layer that ingests bundles from the synthetic playtest corpus, computes design-relevant statistics (median session length, decision points per minute, resource Gini, time-to-first-conflict, dominant strategy distribution, etc.), and tracks these across commits. Regression detection: "the median session length dropped 30% after this commit" gets surfaced automatically.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
What it unlocks: a meaningful definition of "regression" for emergent behavior, which unit tests can't capture. Designers and agents share a common quantitative vocabulary for "is the game still doing what we want."
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
### Scenario library (continuous, no spec)
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
The convention that every annotated bug bundle gets promoted to a permanent regression scenario. Implemented incrementally as part of Specs 1, 3, and 4. The library compounds: it becomes the project's institutional memory of "what's known to be hard."
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
## Tier 2 ╨ô?" Multipliers
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
Tier 1 makes AI-first possible. Tier 2 makes it powerful.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
### Spec 9: AI Playtester Agent
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
Status: **Proposed.**
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
What it delivers: a separate LLM-driven agent that plays the game (via the same `submit()` boundary), then writes natural-language qualitative feedback ("I found myself doing X repetitively in the early game; the second hour felt aimless"). Distinct from coding agents ╨ô?" its job is to *play and report*, not to edit code.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
What it unlocks: the closest approximation to "is it fun?" that doesn't require a human. Combined with Spec 8's quantitative metrics, the design loop closes.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
Why it depends on Spec 3: the playtester is just a specific class of policy plugged into the synthetic harness, plus an LLM-driven post-run report.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
### Spec 7: Bundle Search / Corpus Index
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
Status: **Proposed.**
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
What it delivers: an index over the bundle corpus with structured query: "show me all sessions where pathfinding flagged stuck units in the first 1000 ticks," "find sessions with high decision-point variance," "find sessions where the player's resource balance crashed below threshold X." Bundle metadata is indexed; bundle content is queryable on demand via the replayer.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
What it unlocks: the corpus stops being a folder of files and becomes a query surface for both agents and humans.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
Why it depends on Specs 3 and 4: the corpus needs to exist (3) and be navigable (4) before indexing it earns its keep.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
### Anomaly detection over the corpus (continuous, no spec)
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
A continuous capability that surfaces statistical outliers in tick timing, state divergences, surprise event sequences, etc. Implemented incrementally on top of Specs 7 and 8. The agent surfaces these and investigates without prompting.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
## Tier 3 ╨ô?" Productivity Tooling
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
Tier 3 is leverage on top of an already-working autonomous loop. Defer until Tier 1 and 2 are mature.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
### Spec 4: Standalone Bundle Viewer
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
Status: **Proposed.**
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
What it delivers: a separate package (in this repo, sibling to engine sources) that loads bundles, scrubs a timeline, jumps to markers, diffs state between any two ticks, and replays into a paused World. Includes a programmatic agent-driver API: `bundle.atMarker(id).state(...).events(...).diffSince(...)`. UI optional in v1; CLI / library is sufficient.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
What it unlocks: human productivity. Agents can drive the bundle programmatically without it; humans benefit from the GUI scrubber.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
Why it depends on Spec 1: the viewer reads bundles.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
### Spec 2: Game-Side Annotation UI
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
Status: **Proposed.**
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
What it delivers: in-game hotkey + annotation form + drawing tools (entity selection, region lasso, suggested-path arrow, freehand scribble, screenshot capture). Resolves visual gestures to engine references (entity IDs, world coordinates) at annotation time, attaching the resolved refs to the marker. Free-text and screenshot blob travel as supplementary attachments. Game-specific code per game; this spec defines the conventions.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
What it unlocks: rich, structured human bug reports. Player annotations populate the scenario library (Tier 1).
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
Why it depends on Spec 1: the marker schema is engine-side; the UI just produces markers.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
### Spec 5: Counterfactual Replay / Fork
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
Status: **Proposed.**
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
What it delivers: `SessionReplayer.forkAt(tick).substitute(commands).run()` ╨ô?" change inputs at tick N, replay forward, observe how the simulation diverges from the original. Two-bundle diff utility for visualizing divergence. Substitution semantics, divergence detection, replay-fork tree.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
What it unlocks: the most powerful debugging primitive. "If the player had done X instead of Y, what would have happened?" becomes a single API call.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
Why it's deferred: high architectural complexity (input substitution, divergence representation, fork trees), and the agent's main debugging workflow (load, jump to marker, inspect, step) is fully served by Spec 1's `openAt`. Build it when synthetic playtest reveals concrete counterfactual queries the agent wants to issue.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
### Spec 6: Engine Strict-Mode Determinism Enforcement
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
Status: **Proposed.** Independent of the other specs in this roadmap.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
What it delivers: `World({ strict: true })` flag that rejects mutations from outside system phases. All external state changes must go through `submit()`. Includes escape hatches for setup, deserialization, and explicit out-of-tick maintenance. Auditing of all mutation methods to gate on inside-tick state.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
What it unlocks: structural enforcement of the determinism contract that Spec 1 only documents. Replays can no longer silently diverge ╨ô?" violations throw at the source.
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
Why it's deferred: it's a meaty engine-wide behavioral change with its own design problem (escape hatches, migration, false-positive risk for legitimate setup code). Best handled as a focused spec when its costs and benefits can be evaluated standalone. Spec 1's `selfCheck()` provides 80% of the safety with 0% of the engine surgery in the meantime.

System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
## Suggested Build Order
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
1. Spec 1 (recording & replay) ╨ô?" substrate for everything.
2. Spec 3 (synthetic playtest) ╨ô?" turns recording from "improve human bug reports" into "infinite autonomous bug discovery." Highest leverage.
3. Spec 8 (behavioral metrics) ╨ô?" pairs with Spec 3 to define regressions for emergent behavior.
4. Spec 2 (game-side annotation UI) ╨ô?" humans plug into the same system; game-specific work that can ship in parallel with Spec 4.
5. Spec 4 (standalone viewer) ╨ô?" productivity multiplier for both agents and humans.
6. Spec 7 (corpus index) ╨ô?" once corpus is large enough that browsing it linearly hurts.
7. Spec 9 (AI playtester) ╨ô?" once Specs 3 and 8 are mature enough to drive qualitative feedback usefully.
8. Spec 5 (counterfactual) ╨ô?" once concrete counterfactual queries emerge from agent workflows.
9. Spec 6 (strict-mode) ╨ô?" independent, can ship at any point. Schedule based on determinism-bug pain.

# Task Group: idle-life HUD build-card DOM stability and render-store updates
scope: narrow `idle-life` HUD bugfixes where tick-driven render-store updates can destabilize build-card interaction state, plus the regression/doc pattern that keeps those fixes honest
applies_to: cwd=C:\Users\38909\Documents\github\idle-life; reuse_rule=reuse for HUD/build-drawer/render-store UI bugs in this checkout, but do not generalize the `JSON.stringify` cache key beyond the current flat `ShopCard` model without re-checking the data shape

## User preferences
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
- when the user reports a terse UI defect like "The build item cards keep flickering on mouse hover." -> default to the smallest behavior-preserving fix for the visible bug before exploring redesigns or adjacent HUD polish [Task 1]
- when the defect is narrowly scoped, keep the diff focused on the broken interaction contract rather than bundling broader UI cleanup into the same pass [Task 1]
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
## Reusable knowledge
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
- `src/client/ui/hud.ts` rebuilds the build-card grid from render-store updates, so native CSS hover can flicker if `buildGrid.replaceChildren(...)` runs on every tick even when the visible shop state is unchanged [Task 1]
- `ShopCard` is a flat primitive-only model in this code path, so `JSON.stringify(shopCards)` is a safe dirtiness key for this specific HUD cache [Task 1]
- the landed fix was to cache the last visible shop-card signature in the HUD controller closure and skip the DOM rebuild when that signature is unchanged, while still rebuilding on real visible-state changes [Task 1]
- the regression shape that matched the user-visible bug was "preserves simulated hover state across repeated identical updates"; a companion regression also proved that placement-selection changes still refresh the active card state [Task 1]
- preserving the build drawer DOM while hidden is safe here because the drawer stays mounted across close/reopen cycles in the current HUD architecture [Task 1]
- this repo treated the docs as part of the fix: `docs/learning/lessons.md`, `docs/devlog/summary.md`, and `docs/devlog/detailed/2026-04-21_2026-04-21.md` were updated alongside the code and tests [Task 1]
- verification for the accepted state was `npx vitest run`, `npx tsc --noEmit`, and `npx vite build`; the fix was committed as `cd3b88e` while leaving an unrelated untracked `assets/` directory alone [Task 1]
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
## Failures and how to do differently
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
- symptom: build cards flicker on hover during normal HUD updates -> cause: the build grid DOM is recreated on every render-store tick, which resets native hover under the cursor -> fix: preserve the existing card DOM when the serialized visible `ShopCard` state is unchanged [Task 1]
- symptom: the first regression feels brittle or fails for the wrong reason -> cause: raw DOM-identity assertions (`toBe`) do not directly capture the user-visible hover contract -> fix: assert that a simulated hover marker survives identical updates instead [Task 1]
- symptom: a custom signature helper adds avoidable complexity for this cache -> cause: overengineering the dirtiness check -> fix: prefer `JSON.stringify` while `ShopCard` stays flat and primitive-only [Task 1]
- symptom: focus/hover can still reset on real visible-state changes -> cause: the current fix only preserves DOM for unchanged card state -> fix: if that contract becomes important, follow up with keyed or in-place card updates instead of another full rebuild path [Task 1]
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException

System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
## Reusable knowledge
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
- `World.onDestroy()` / `offDestroy()` already exist and fire before component removal, so they are the clean lifecycle hook for occupancy cleanup owned by a higher-level binding [Task 1]
- `src/index.ts` exports `occupancy-grid.ts`, so occupancy changes become public API changes once added there [Task 1]
- `OccupancyBinding` is the higher-level abstraction that should own blocker metadata (`kind`), whole-cell occupancy, optional sub-cell crowding, and destroy-time cleanup while delegating low-level storage to `OccupancyGrid` / `SubcellOccupancyGrid` [Task 1]
- `getCellStatus()` exposes `blockedBy`, `crowdedBy`, and `freeSubcellSlots`, which lets repo code distinguish building/resource/unit-style blockers without maintaining parallel grids [Task 1]
- benchmark output that only reports world/path timing is not enough for RTS occupancy decisions; `scripts/rts-benchmark.mjs` should also report occupancy workloads and counters [Task 1]
- `createGridPathCacheKey()` must include `movingEntity` whenever passability can change under ignore-self semantics [Task 1]
- `aoe2/docs/engine-feedback/current.md` should show only active asks; once the engine work is complete, move the closed item into `past.md` [Task 1]
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
## Failures and how to do differently
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
- symptom: occupancy API exists but repo code still has to compose low-level grids and cleanup manually -> cause: there is no lifecycle-owning binding or blocker metadata -> fix: add a higher-level `OccupancyBinding` with `world.onDestroy()` cleanup and cell-status metadata [Task 1]
- symptom: passability appears crowding-aware but `reserve()` still succeeds in crowded cells -> cause: `reserve()` bypasses the same guard used by `block()` / `occupy()` -> fix: gate `reserve()` through the crowding checks too and add a regression test [Task 1]
- symptom: cached paths are reused across different moving entities -> cause: `createGridPathCacheKey()` omitted `movingEntity` -> fix: include it in the key and cover it in `tests/path-service.test.ts` [Task 1]
- symptom: benchmarking cannot show whether occupancy work is viable at RTS scale -> cause: only world/path timings are reported -> fix: add explicit occupancy workload summaries and scan counters to the benchmark harness [Task 1]
- symptom: review automation does not complete because Gemini/Codex reviewer tooling is unavailable -> cause: model availability/quota issues in the local CLI -> fix: record the blocker explicitly and rely on direct tests/benchmarks plus targeted regression coverage instead of implying the reviews succeeded [Task 1]
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException

System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
## Reusable knowledge
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
- `src/nav.rs` is the source of truth for supported image extensions; navigation, scans, and file-dialog filters should stay aligned through that list [Task 1]
- `src/decode.rs` uses `rawler` for RAW decode, with different fallback behavior for library thumbnails versus Detail loads [Task 1]
- RAW inputs should save edited output as PNG copies (`*_edited.png`) rather than attempting RAW re-encode; the relevant helpers are `edited_save_path()` and `save_edited_image()` [Task 1]
- `EditState` carries rotation as quarter turns, and rotation participates in undo/redo/reset like the other edits [Task 2]
- live preview rotation and saved-output rotation both depend on the same quarter-turn math; `src/edit.rs`, `src/viewer.rs`, and `assets/shaders/image.wgsl` must stay in sync [Task 2]
- in this app, the user-visible thumbnail containment contract lives at the `iced` widget layer; `Image::content_fit(iced::ContentFit::Contain)` should be applied on the thumbnail widget itself, not inferred from decoded image dimensions [Task 4]
- the shared square-slot seam is `thumbnail_slot_with_renderer(...)` plus the thin production wrapper `thumbnail_slot(...)`, and both Library cards and drag previews should reuse that helper to keep containment behavior consistent [Task 4]
- renderer-backed draw-bounds regressions for wide, tall, and square images are the durable proof that thumbnail containment still holds [Task 4]
- `DetailLoadState` centralizes request id, loading stage, preview visibility, and EXIF readiness for staged RAW loads [Task 3]
- the staged RAW Detail path is: embedded preview first when available, then full decode plus EXIF only for the still-current request; stale preview/full/EXIF completions are ignored by request ID [Task 3]
- save/export must stay blocked while only a preview is visible or while auto lens metadata is still pending [Task 3]
- repo-required docs updates for this area included `docs/architecture/ARCHITECTURE.md`, `docs/architecture/decisions.md`, `docs/architecture/drift-log.md`, `docs/devlog/summary.md`, `docs/devlog/detailed/...`, and `docs/learning/lessons.md` [Task 1][Task 3][Task 4]
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
## Failures and how to do differently
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
- symptom: RAW tests claim branch coverage that the fixtures do not actually distinguish -> cause: thumbnail/preview/full-image/thumbnail-only cases are collapsed into too few fixtures -> fix: use distinct fixtures for each fallback branch and only claim the branches the fixtures prove [Task 1]
- symptom: docs drift from the implementation's real fallback order -> cause: documentation was updated before the code path fully settled -> fix: refresh docs after the code is stable and use wording that matches the exact fallback contract [Task 1]
- symptom: clippy fails on a small helper refactor after broader feature work -> cause: helper cleanup was not re-run through clippy early -> fix: rerun `cargo clippy -- -D warnings` soon after touching shared helpers [Task 1]
- symptom: rotation behavior can drift across preview and save paths -> cause: quarter-turn semantics are split across save logic, viewer geometry, and shader UV handling -> fix: centralize the transform rules if this area expands [Task 2]
- symptom: preview-to-full swap causes a large zoom jump -> cause: a resolution-based zoom rewrite tried to recompute framing from source dimensions -> fix: preserve the current zoom/pan and let viewer fit math handle size differences [Task 3]
- symptom: automated reviews do not finish because `codex exec review uncommitted` reconnects fail or Gemini returns repeated `429` capacity exhaustion -> cause: external service/tooling instability -> fix: record review coverage as partial instead of completed and rely on direct validation plus targeted regressions [Task 3]
- symptom: thumbnail tests drift into production-generic plumbing and become hard to trust -> cause: the harness is too indirect for a narrow rendering contract -> fix: keep generic renderer plumbing minimal and drive the contract through a thin production wrapper [Task 4]
- symptom: a fallback path can silently stretch thumbnails in release -> cause: containment is enforced only in tests or helper-adjacent code -> fix: remove fallback behavior that bypasses the explicit `ContentFit::Contain` contract [Task 4]
- symptom: full-suite validation fails at `decode::tests::write_decoded_cache_triggers_periodic_pruning` while the thumbnail change looks sound -> cause: an intermittent unrelated repo flake -> fix: rerun cleanly before treating the validation result as final, and record the flake as unrelated instead of misattributing it to the thumbnail fix [Task 4]

## Reusable knowledge
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
- milestone 1 was explicitly scoped to: one resident, desktop companion window, autonomous side-view traversal, mouse-only management, no jumping, no day/night cycle, no offline progress, no relationships, and real-time-only simulation [Task 1]
- the starter careers and basic house/build loop constraints were locked: Writer, Artist, Programmer; indoor-only freeform placement; all needs important but non-fatal; hunger-first; sell returns half price [Task 1]
- `civ-engine` docs show the engine is deterministic, headless, ECS-based, command/event driven, and grid-based, so "freeform" should be interpreted as fine-grid placement in simulation with smooth rendering handled separately [Task 2]
- the chosen runtime shape was worker-hosted `World`, renderer/UI on the main thread, commands/events/diffs between them, and headless scenario/debug verification via `WorldDebugger` / `runScenario()` [Task 2]
- behavior trees are a good fit for resident autonomy because they are shared-blueprint, per-entity-state, and serializable [Task 2]
- shell-level `Escape` handling should prioritize the confirm dialog, then placement cancellation; `confirmDialog.isOpen()` and `dismiss()` make that precedence explicit [Task 3]
- a focusable shell root (`tabIndex = -1`) plus focus-on-primary-pointer interaction makes shell-scoped keyboard handling reliable [Task 3]
- `placementMode` should be a small data type plus controller in `src/client/placement-mode.ts` and `src/client/placement-mode-controller.ts`, not state buried inside the HUD module [Task 3]

## User preferences
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
- when the user says "I am building a news console website. Ask me questions and help me iterate on what I want. Consolidate into design/spec.md when we are done." -> start with focused discovery, then consolidate after scope is clarified [Task 1]
- when the user says "user is myself" and wants news useful for "my curiosity, learning, and investment decision making" that should "Check facts and remove sensational biases" -> default the product/workflow to personal research and de-biasing rather than generic news browsing [Task 1]
- when the user asks for "A blend of bloomberg style and research space" / "Bloomberg" -> default to dense, serious, analytical visual direction in this product family [Task 1]
- when the user says "Also give your options letters so I can easily pick in the future." -> use lettered clarification options for faster replies in this workflow [Task 1]
- when the user says "Crawled daily news articles should be saved by date in a folder." -> preserve transparent date-partitioned filesystem storage as the default [Task 1][Task 2]
- when the user says "Focus on a concrete set of CLI commands and write a plan to implement it and then do it." -> move from abstract product talk to a concrete command contract and execution plan [Task 1][Task 2]
- when the user clarifies "The console should be powered by CLI but should also have a visual website." -> treat dual-surface CLI + website architecture as a hard product requirement [Task 1][Task 2]
- when the user says "keep working until we have the whole app," do not stop at a partial milestone if clear spec gaps remain [Task 3]
- when the user says a command path is "such a long and ugly way to call this tool" and "I need it to be more elegant," prefer a shorter local invocation path rather than explaining the ugly one [Task 4]
- when the user asks "but how does it know what to ingest", explain the ingestion model in terms of source configuration, not just CLI syntax [Task 4]
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
## Reusable knowledge
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
- `design/spec.md` is the product-spec anchor for this repo: it defines a command-based CLI as the control plane, a local website as the reading/analysis surface, RSS-first ingestion, URL import, local-only operation, source metadata for diversity, article-centric organization, and long-term memory [Task 1]
- the spec explicitly defers research boards, multi-user/public accounts, cloud-first operation, paid APIs, ideology scoring, and fully automated truth guarantees; do not quietly re-expand scope back into those areas without a new user ask [Task 1]
- the first scaffold intentionally favored transparent local files over a hidden DB: `data/articles/YYYY-MM-DD/` plus JSON config/index files [Task 2]
- early scaffold files included `package.json`, `tsconfig.json`, `tsconfig.cli.json`, `vite.config.ts`, `index.html`, `scripts/build.mjs`, `docs/ARCHITECTURE.md`, `docs/devlog-summary.md`, `docs/devlog-detailed.md`, `src/shared/*`, `src/cli/index.ts`, `src/web/*`, and `tests/news-cli.test.ts` [Task 2]
- PowerShell `npm` failed because `npm.ps1` was blocked, but `npm.cmd` worked; git status in this repo needed `git -C <path> -c safe.directory=...` because of dubious ownership [Task 2]
- shared support for article annotations, tracked price histories, AI provider config, and website launch helpers lives in `src/shared/*` [Task 3]
- `news web` launches the local website; `news prices sync` writes tracked ticker histories under `data/prices/`; AI tasks use external providers when available but fall back to deterministic local drafts [Task 3]
- digest generation includes linked supporting articles, saved notes/highlights, and assistant sections; website search includes `contentText`, notes, and highlights [Task 3]
- the short local entrypoints are `.\news.cmd ...` from repo root, `npm.cmd run news -- ...`, and bare `news ...` after `npm.cmd link` [Task 4]
- `sources add` determines what gets ingested; `watchlist`, `themes`, and `macros` only affect prioritization after ingestion [Task 4]
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
## Failures and how to do differently
System.Management.Automation.RemoteException
- symptom: the product scope takes too many back-and-forth rounds to lock -> cause: discovery did not front-load the most discriminating questions -> fix: ask early about daily loop, surface model, storage constraints, and the trust/fact model [Task 1]
- symptom: the product gets framed too much as a website -> cause: the dual-surface requirement was not treated as architectural from the start -> fix: treat "CLI-powered but should also have a visual website" as an early product constraint [Task 1][Task 2]
- symptom: large Windows patch operations fail with `CreateProcessAsUserW failed: 206` -> cause: oversized patch payloads in this environment -> fix: split big scaffold edits into smaller patches [Task 2]
- symptom: dependency install and validation remain incomplete -> cause: `npm.cmd install` timed out once and was then aborted by the user -> fix: carry the scaffold as partially validated until a follow-up run completes install, tests, typecheck, and build [Task 2]
- symptom: build/test commands fail with `spawn EPERM` -> cause: sandbox/esbuild spawn restrictions -> fix: rerun outside the sandbox when needed and report the blocker honestly [Task 3]
- symptom: patching docs with mojibake or encoding noise keeps failing -> cause: broken patch context in the existing file -> fix: replace the file cleanly instead of patching line by line [Task 3]
- symptom: tooling tests fail for the nicer CLI path -> cause: the repo-local launcher or `news` script does not actually exist yet -> fix: add the launcher/script first, then rerun `tests/tooling.test.ts` [Task 4]
